# Data Manipulation using Dplyr


```R
library(dplyr)
options(warn=0)
```


```R
college <- read.csv("college_data.csv",stringsAsFactors=TRUE,na.strings=c("","NA"))
```


```R
str(college)
```

    'data.frame':	777 obs. of  19 variables:

```R

```


```R
#how to select the variables from the dataset or dataframe
#using select function
```


```R
subcollege <- select(college, College.name, private, apps, enroll)
names(subcollege)
```


<ol class=list-inline>
	<li>'College.name'</li>
	<li>'private'</li>
	<li>'apps'</li>
	<li>'enroll'</li>
</ol>




```R
#changing the order in which variables occur in new dataset
#by just mentioning them in the order you want
```


```R
subcollege <- select(college, apps, enroll, College.name, private)
```


```R
names(subcollege)
```


<ol class=list-inline>
	<li>'apps'</li>
	<li>'enroll'</li>
	<li>'College.name'</li>
	<li>'private'</li>
</ol>

```R
#dropping or deleting columns by making use of (-) sign
```


```R
subcollege <- select(college, -apps, -enroll, -College.name, -private)
subcollege <- select(college, -c(apps, enroll, College.name, private))
```


```R
subcollege
```

```R
#Selecting all the columns between College.name and phd
#By making use of (:) semicolon
```


```R
subcollege <- select(college, College.name : phd)
```

```R
subcollege
```

```R
#Dropping column names in the same manner
```


```R
subcollege <- select(college, -(College.name : phd))
```


```R
names(subcollege)
```


<ol class=list-inline>
	<li>'terminal'</li>
	<li>'s_f_ratio'</li>
	<li>'perc_alumni'</li>
	<li>'expend'</li>
	<li>'grad_rate'</li>
</ol>




```R
#Selecting variables by giving the column index
```


```R
subcollege <- select(college, 1,2,3,6,7,9)
```


```R
names(subcollege)
```


<ol class=list-inline>
	<li>'College.name'</li>
	<li>'private'</li>
	<li>'apps'</li>
	<li>'top10perc'</li>
	<li>'top25perc'</li>
	<li>'p_undergrad'</li>
</ol>




```R
#Dropping variables by marking (-) sign in front of the index number
```


```R
subcollege <- select(college, -1,-2,-3)
subcollege <- select(college, -c(1,2,3,4))
```


```R
names(subcollege)
```


<ol class=list-inline>
	<li>'enroll'</li>
	<li>'top10perc'</li>
	<li>'top25perc'</li>
	<li>'f_undergrad'</li>
	<li>'p_undergrad'</li>
	<li>'outstate'</li>
	<li>'room_board'</li>
	<li>'books'</li>
	<li>'personal'</li>
	<li>'phd'</li>
	<li>'terminal'</li>
	<li>'s_f_ratio'</li>
	<li>'perc_alumni'</li>
	<li>'expend'</li>
	<li>'grad_rate'</li>
</ol>




```R
#Selecting all the columns between 4 and 8 by making
#making use of (:) semicolon
```


```R
subcollege <- select(college, 4:8)
```


```R
names(subcollege)
```


<ol class=list-inline>
	<li>'accept'</li>
	<li>'enroll'</li>
	<li>'top10perc'</li>
	<li>'top25perc'</li>
	<li>'f_undergrad'</li>
</ol>




```R
subcollege <- select(college, -(4:8))
```


```R
names(subcollege)
```

	<li>'College.name'</li>
	<li>'private'</li>
	<li>'apps'</li>

```R
#Renaming variables using select() function
```


```R
subcollege <- select(college, "colgname" = College.name, 2,3,6,7 )
names(subcollege)
```


<ol class=list-inline>
	<li>'colgname'</li>
	<li>'private'</li>
	<li>'apps'</li>
	<li>'top10perc'</li>
	<li>'top25perc'</li>
</ol>




```R
#But it is recommended to use rename() function
```


```R
newcollege <- rename(college, "colgname" = College.name)
names(newcollege)
```


<ol class=list-inline>
	<li>'colgname'</li>
	<li>'private'</li>
	<li>'apps'</li>
	<li>'accept'</li>
	<li>'enroll'</li>
	<li>'top10perc'</li>
	<li>'top25perc'</li>

```R
#Applying multiple filters with "AND" logic using "," or "&" sign
college_sub <- filter(college, private == "No", grad_rate > 50 )
college_sub <- filter(college, private == "No" & grad_rate > 50 )
```


```R
college_sub
```

```R
college_sub <- filter(college, private!="No" , grad_rate > 50, terminal <78, phd > 50)
```


```R
college_sub
```

```R
#Applying multiple filters with "OR" logic using "|" sign
college_sub <- filter(college, private!="No"|grad_rate>50, phd>70)
```


```R
college_sub
```

```R
#The above filtering can be achieved by using [] brackets
#however this is very verbose as one has to follow data$variable name format
```


```R
college_sub <- college[(college$private == "No" & college$grad_date > 50) ,]
```


```R
college_sub
```

```R
#Creating new variables which are functions of existinf variables using mutate() function
```


```R
newcollege <- mutate(college,
                  newenroll = enroll/10,
                  notaccept = apps - accept)
```

```R
#In case you are only interested in the new variables and you only want them to be in
#your dataset then you can use transmute() function
```


```R
newcollege1 <- transmute(college,
                         newenroll = enroll/10,
                         notaccept = apps - accept)
```


```R
newcollege1
```

```R
#An example of using if_else() function with mutate() function
```


```R
college_1 <- mutate(college,
                 newenroll = if_else(phd <= 75, "belowAvg", "aboveAvg"),
                 notaccept = apps - accept)
```


```R
college_1
```

```R
#if_else() function is faster than ifelse() function
#It handles the missing values.
#Unlike ifelse() function, if_else() function retains the data type 
```


```R
#ifelse() function
system.time(ifelse(college$grad_rate > 50, "Goodscore", "Badscore"))
```


       user  system elapsed 
          0       0       0 



```R
#if_else() function
system.time(if_else(college$grad_rate > 50, "Goodscore", "Badscore"))
```


       user  system elapsed 
          0       0       0

```R
x <- factor(sample(letters[1:5], 10, replace = TRUE))
class(x)
```

'factor'



```R
class(ifelse(x %in% c("a","b","c"), x , factor(NA)))
class(if_else(x %in% c("a","b","c"), x , factor(NA)))
```

```R
#To get the summary statistics
```


```R
colgsummary <- summarise(college,
                        count = n(),
                        avgaccept=mean(accept, na.rm = TRUE),
                        sdaccept = sd(accept, na.rm = TRUE),
                        mediaaccept = median(accept, na.rm = TRUE),
                        Q3rd = quantile(accept, .75)
                        )
```


```R
#If you wish to look into the groups based upon th levels of use of a particular variable, using group_by() function
#Functions like select(), filter(), mutate(), slice(), summarise() etc become more powerful when you apply it
#on the object generated by group_by function.
```


```R
groupprivatecollege <- group_by(college, private)
```

```R
colgsummary1 <- summarise(groupprivatecollege,
                        count = n(),
                        avgaccept=mean(accept, na.rm = TRUE),
                        sdaccept = sd(accept, na.rm = TRUE),
                        mediaaccept = median(accept, na.rm = TRUE),
                        Q3rd = quantile(accept, .75)
                        )
```
